Jamison Brereton

24 (644)
Indra
Vi┼Ыvamanas Vaiya┼Ыva
30 verses: uс╣гс╣Зih (except anuс╣гс╣нubh 30), arranged in trcas ╠е
The first twenty-seven verses of this hymn are dedicated to Indra, while the final tr╠еca (vss. 28тАУ30) is a d─Бnastuti of the patron Varo Suс╣г─Бman, with Dawn the divinity addressed because of her association with the distribution of the priestly gift. The first two verses of the d─Бnastuti are unexceptional in diction and tone, but the last verse (30) contains puns and neologisms, as often in d─Бnastutis.
The rest of the hymn contains fairly standard praise of Indra, with special emphasis on his generosityтАФr─Б╠Бdhas тАЬgenerosityтАЭ is something of a signature word in the hymn, occurring six timesтАФthough his powers do not go unmentioned. The need to praise Indra to stimulate his giving is also a recurrent motif in the hymn, and the poet calls upon both himself (sometimes by name) and his companions to provide that praise (see, e.g., vss. 1, 14, 19, 22тАУ23). Such interactivity was also char
acteristic of the preceding hymn (VIII.23) to Agni.
The hymn consists of tr╠еcas, but there is little unity within most of these triplets; instead, there are a number of instances of cross-tr╠еca transitions (see, e.g., vss. 3/4, 6/7, 9/10). The poet also makes considerable use of alliteration and, especially, of pairing derivationally related words. Verse 10 provides a particularly fine example of the latter practice.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬLet us earnestly, friends, address our prayer to Indra, the wielder of the thunderbolt, for you I praise thechief leader (in battles), the resolute (opposer of foes).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Comrades, we direct our formulation to Indra who bears the maceтАФ I shall praise him on your behalfтАФto the most manly, bold one.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Geldner takes stuс╣г├й here as an infinitive, but the nearby parallels he cites (VIII.21.9, 23.7) are unaccented and clearly 1st person. The switch between 1st pl. (─Б╠Б ┼Ыiс╣г─Бmahi) and 1st sg. (stuс╣г├й) is not unusual in this kind of context, where the poet speaks in the 1st plural jointly for himself and his fellow ritual performers and in the 1st singular for himself alone, with a 2nd pl. address to those same comrades (vaс╕е in b).

Griffith

COMPANIONS, let us learn a prayer to Indra. whom the thunder arms,
To glorify your bold and most heroic Friend.

Geldner

Genossen! Wir w├╝nschen fein dem Keulentr├дger Indra eine Erbauung zu singen f├╝r euch, dem Mannhaftesten, K├╝hnen.

Grassmann

O Freunde, lasst uns ein Gebet dem blitzbewehrten Indra weihn; Gern sing’ ich eurem tapfersten, dem muthigen.

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬYou are renowned for strength; from the slaying of Vс╣Ыtra, you are (famed as) Vс╣Ыtrahan; you surpass,hero, the opulent in the donation of your riches.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

For you are famed because of your swelling might and, as Vr╠еtra-smasher, because of your Vr╠еtra-smashing [/obstacle-smashing].
With your bounties you outdo the bounteous ones in piety, o champion.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Two etymological figures: vс╣Ыtrah├бtyena vс╣Ыtrah─Б╠Б(b) and magha├нr magh├│naс╕е (c).

On the unusual construction of ├бti тИЪd─Б┼Ы see comm. ad VI.16.20.

For thou by slaying Vrtra art the Vrtra-slayer, famed for might.
Thou, Hero, in rich gifts surpassest wealthy chiefs.

English translation:

тАЬPraised by us, bestow upon us riches of wonderful variety; you, the lord of steeds, who, at the issue (ofyour weapons) put your enemies to flight, are the donor (of treasures).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

At the issue of the weapons: nireke cidvasuс╕е = tav─Бyudhanirgaman─Бd eva ┼Ыatravaс╕е pal─Бyante

Being praised, bring here to us wealth that offers most brilliant fameтАФ you who are exclusively the good giver, o master of the fallow bays.

As such, when glorified, bring us riches of very wondrous fame,
Set in the highest rank, Wealth-giver, Lord of Bays!

English translation:

тАЬBurst open to your worshippers, Indra, the highly prized wealth; glorified by us, do you who areendowed with resolution, bring (us wealth) with a resolute (mind).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Tear out what is exclusive and dear to the peoples, Indra.
Being praised, bring it here boldly, bold one.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Another figure: dhс╣Ыс╣гat─Б╠Бdhс╣Ыс╣гс╣Зo.

This verse echoes vs. 3 in reverse order: 3a st├бv─Бno ─Б╠Бbhara / 3c nirek├бm // 4a nirek├бm / 4c st├бvam─Бna ─Б╠Бbhara. These echoes straddle a tс╣Ыca boundary.

Griffith

Yea, Indra, thou disclosest that preeminent dear wealth of men:
Boldly, O Bold One, glorified, bring it to us.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬLord of steeds, in the recovery of the cattle the opponents resist not your left hand nor your right, yourenemies (resist you) not.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Hindrances obstruct neither your left nor your right hand,
nor do repulsions, o master of the fallow bays, in your quests for
cattle.

Jamison Brereton Notes

тАЬhindrancesтАЭ (─Бm├║raс╕е) and тАЬrepulsionsтАЭ (parib─Б╠Бdhaс╕е) are complementary notions, the equivalent of тАЬthrust and parryтАЭ (or rather parry and thrust).

Unfortunately they do not go well into English, esp. in the plural. On ─Бm├║r- see Scarlatta 391-92.

Griffith

The workers of destruction stay neither thy right hand nor thy left:
Nor hosts that press about thee, Lord of Bays, in fight.

Geldner

Hindernisse und Fallstricke halten nicht deine linke noch deine rechte Hand ab auf den Rinderjagden, o Falbenlenker.

Grassmann

Nicht wehren deine rechte Hand, die linke nicht die Feinde ab, Noch die Bedr├дnger in der Schlacht, o Rosseherr.

Elizarenkova

тАЬI approach you, thunderer, with praises, as (a cowherd goes) with cattle to the pasture; gratify thedesire, satisfy the mind of your adorer.тАЭ

I fit you out with my songs, as a pen with cows, o master of the stones. Fulfill the desire and the mind of the singer.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMay we, hero, slayer of Vс╣Ыtra, invoked of many become possessed of this your new, desirable, andhappiness producing wealth.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

O Vr╠еtra-smasher, o champion, might we know of this newer,
eagerly sought generosity of yours, o good one, much-invoked.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The opening word of c, v├бso, is read as v├бsoс╕е by the Pp., followed by Oldenberg and Geldner - that is, with the loss of underlying final -s before the cluster sp- – hence a gen. sg. belonging with the long gen. sg. noun phrase ending with r─Б╠Бdhasaс╕е. This is of course possible, but the presence of undoubted voc. vaso in 7c in a hymn that is over-partial to vocatives and given to repetitions across verses, supports a voc. interpretation here.

Griffith

May we, O Vrtra-slayer, O Hero, find this thy newest boon, Longed-for, and excellent, thou who art much invoked!

Geldner

Wir m├╢chten diese deine neueste, g├╝tige, begehrenswerte Freigebigkeit kennen lernen, tapferer Vritrat├╢ter, Vielgerufener.

Grassmann

Wir m├╢gen dies begehrte Gut, dein neustes, reichstes, Vritrafeind, Erlangen, vielgerufener, o starker Held.

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬAs, Indra, inspirer (of men), your strength is irresistible, (so) invoked of many, your munificence to thedonor (of oblations) cannot be marred.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Inspirer of men: nс╣Ыto = voc. of nс╣Ыtu, dancer, or who causes to dance, i.e.,agitator, exciter; from Indra’s faculty of internal impulse in all beings, sarvasya antary─Бmitay─Б nartayitaс╕е

Jamison Brereton

For, Indra, just as for you there exists a swelling might that cannot be encompassed, o dancer,
your giving to the pious man cannot be impaired, o
much-invoked one.

Griffith

O Indra, Dancer, Much-invoked! as thy great power is unsurpassed,
So be thy bounty to the worshipper unchecked.

Geldner

Denn wie deine Kraft unerreicht ist, o T├дnzer Indra, so sei deine Gabe f├╝r den Spender ungeschm├дlert, Vielgerufener.

Grassmann

Denn wie dir unbezwungne Kraft, o vielgerufner Indra, ist, So sei dem Frommen unversehrte Gab’, o Held.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMost adorable, chief leader (of men), invigorate (yourself with the Soma) for (the conquest of) greatwealth; consume, Maghavan, the strong (cities of the asuras) for the rich spoil.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Rain yourself down, o you who are greater than great, o best of men, for great generosity.
Being yourself steadfast, stand fast, bounteous one, for bounteous
giving.

Jamison Brereton Notes

A verse full of figures: mah─Бmaha, mah├й (ab), dс╣Ыс╕╖h├б┼Ы cid dс╣Ыhya (c), maghavan magh├бttaye. There is also an inter-tс╣Ыca echo between voc. nс╣Ыto (9b) and voc. nс╣Ыtama (10b), with nс╣Ыto returning in 12a.

Griffith

Most Mighty, most heroic One, for mighty bounty fill thee full.
Though strong, strengthen thyself to win wealth, Maghavan!

Grassmann

Zu grosser Spende schl├╝rfe nun, grossm├дchtigster, gewaltigster, Sei stark, o starker, reich, um Reichthum zu verleihn.

Pour here the drop for Indra: he will drink the somian honey.
He will spur himself on in his generosity and greatness.

With bounty and with majesty will he further us.

English translation:

тАЬLet me address the lord of steeds, who associates his strength (with the Maruts); now hear the words ofthe son of Vya┼Ыva praising you.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Dakс╣гam = radhaс╕е;

A┼Ыvya = the son of A┼Ыva, or Vya┼Ыva

Jamison Brereton

I have addressed the lord of the fallow bays as he engorges his skill. Now listen to the son of A┼Ыva as he praises.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The expression d├бkс╣гam pс╣Ы├▒c├бntam is somewhat peculiar, and Geldner takes the two words as separate qualifiers of Indra: тАЬdem Verst├дndigen, Spendenden.тАЭ However, I.141.1 bh├бgaс╣Г d├бkс╣гaс╣Г n├б papr╠еc─Бsi suggests that d├бkс╣гam should be the object of the pres. participle. By the tr. тАЬengorging skillтАЭ I mean that Indra fills his latent quality (skill) with energy (perhaps derived from soma and praise) and makes it available to use.

Acdg. to the Anukramaс╣З─л, our poet Vi┼Ыvamanas has the patronymic Vaiya┼Ыva (vs. 23), that is, son of Vya┼Ыva (тАШwithout horsesтАЩ), and the poet mentions his family in vss. 22, 28-29 with the distracted stem vi ya┼Ыva-. But in this verse he refers to himself instead as a┼Ыvi y├б-, also distracted, which, on the one hand, is simply an anagram of the family name with the first two syllables reversed, but, on the other, credits him with possession of (or at least relationship to) horses, whereas the unmetathesized version announces him as horse-less.

Griffith

I spake to the Bay Coursers’ Lord, to him who gives ability:
Now hear the son of Asva as he praises thee.

Geldner

Ich habe dem Herrn der Falben zugeredet, dem Verst├дndigen, Spendenden. H├╢re nun auch auf den S├дnger, den Asvinschen!

Grassmann

Ich rief den Herrn der F├╝chse an, ihn, welcher T├╝chtigkeit verleiht; So h├╢re nun den preisenden, des A├зva Sohn.

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬNo one, Indra, has ever been born more mighty than you, no one (surpassing you) in riches; no one(more powerful) in protection; no one (more entitled) to praise.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

For surely never before has a greater hero than you been born,
neither in wealthтАФnot in just such a way (as you are)тАФnor in favor.

Jamison Brereton Notes

On the lexeme y├║jy─Бya тИЪvс╣Э see comm. ad IX.88.1.

The expression na├нv├бth─Б (that is, n├б ev├бth─Б), placed between the two instrumentals, is opaque: ev├бth─Б is a hapax. Oldenberg helpfully adduces IV.30.1 n├бkir indra tv├бd ├║ttaraс╕е .. .n├бkir ev─Б╠Бy├бth─Б tv├бm тАЬThere is no one higher than you, Indra тАж no one who is exactly as you are,тАЭ and our ev├бth─Б appears almost to be a blend of ev─Б╠Б y├бth─Б or some abbreviation thereof.

Griffith

Never was any Hero born before thee mightier than thou:
None certairdy like thee in goodness and in wealth.

Geldner

Denn sicherlich wurde auch fr├╝her niemals ein gr├╢├Яerer Held als du geboren; nicht an Reichtum, noch von solcher Art, noch l├╢blichem Werke.

Grassmann

Denn wahrlich nimmer auch zuvor erstand ein st├дrkerer als du, Noch der dir gleich an Reichthum sei und Herrlichkeit.

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬPour out, priest, the most exhilarating (draught) of the sweet (sacrificial) Soma, for he, the ever-mightyhero, alone is praised.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

(Pour) right here what is more invigorating than honey, or pour, Adhvaryu, (what is more invigorating) than the stalk,
for in this way the ever-strengthening hero is praised.

Jamison Brereton Notes

I supply si├▒c├б from b as the verb also of a, and supply mad├нntaram of a as the object of b, with ├бndhasaс╕е dependent on it as m├бdhvaс╕е is in a. Geldner by contrast (fld. by Klein DGRV II.183) supplies тАЬbringтАЭ in a and takes ├бndhasaс╕е as a partitive genitive in b. This is not impossible, but my interpretation requires less extraneous material.

Another cross-tс╣Ыca connection: ev─Б╠Бin c echoes ev├бth─Б in 15c. More cleverly, 16ab ├йd u m(├бdhvo)тАж si├▒c├б picks up 13a ├йndum тАж si├▒cata (note that ├йdum and ├йndum are almost identical).

Griffith

O ministering priest, pour out of the sweet juice what gladdens most:
So is the Hero praised who ever prospers us.

Geldner

Bring den Soma her, der berauschender als Met ist, oder schenke von dem Trank ein, Adhvaryu, denn so wird der Held gepriesen, der stets Gedeihliche.

Grassmann

Den giess nun ein, o Opferer, der mehr berauscht als Meth und Seim, Denn so ja hat ihn gern der Held, der stets erquickt.

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬIndra, ruler of horses, no one surpasses your ancient praise, either for force or for fame.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

None ismightier or more praiseworthy (or richer) than you

Jamison Brereton

O Indra, mounter of the fallow bays, none has reached up to your foremost praise hymn
in swelling strength nor in favor.

Griffith

Indra, whom Tawny Coursers bear, praise such as thine, preeminent,

English translation:

тАЬCome, freinds, let us glorify Indra, the leader, who is entitled to praise, who, single, overcomes allhostile hosts.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Come now! Comrades, let us praise Indra, the superior man worthy of praise,
who all alone surmounts all the separate peoples.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The a p─Бda is repeated twice elsewhere in VIII: 81.4, 95.7. The reason for the accent on st├бv─Бma, which does not begin the p─Бda and probably not its clause, is unclear, though it may well be connected with its relationship with the exhortative 2nd pl. impv. ├йta тАЬcome on!тАЭ It would, in fact, be possible to construe ├нndram with ├йta n├║ and begin a new clause with st├бv─Бma (тАЬCome now to Indra; let us praise the superior manтАжтАЭ), but this seems unnatural. It is curious that Oldenberg does not comment on the accent here or in the other passages.

Griffith

Come, sing we praise to Indra, friends, the Hero who deserves the laud,
Him who with none to aid o’ercomes all tribes of men.

English translation:

тАЬRecite agreeable words, sweeter than clarified butter, or than Soma, to the illustrious (Indra), who isgratified by eulogy, who rejects not praise.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

For the heaven-ruling one who does not withhold cattle, who seeks cattle, speak a wondrous speech,
sweeter than ghee and honey,

Griffith

To him who wins the kine, who keeps no cattle back, Celestial God,
Speak wondrous speech more sweet than butter and than meath.

English translation:

тАЬGlorify Indra, the unassailable, the powerful, the regulator (of man), as was done by Vya┼Ыva, he, thelord, gives a spacious dwelling to the donor (of the oblation).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Donor: yamam = stotс╣Ыbhiс╕е suniyatam, who isconciliated by his praisers; maс╣Гham─Бnam gayam = honourale wealth; or, a house for the worship of the gods

Jamison Brereton

Like Vya┼Ыva, praise Indra, who controls the prizewinning (horse) that rides the wave,
liberally apportioning the property of the stranger to the pious man.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Here as elsewhere (II.5.1, III.27.3, both with pl. v─Бj├нnaс╕е) y├бmam governs the accusative.

Griffith

As Vyasva did, praise Indra, praise the Strong unfluctuating Guide,
Who gives the foe’s possessions to the worshipper.

Geldner

Preise du wie Vyasva den Indra, der das wellenbegleitete Rennpferd lenkt, der an den Opferspender das Besitztum des Geldprotzen verteilt.

Grassmann

Preis’ Indra nach Via├зva’s Art, den starken Lenker, der nicht wankt, Der dem Verehrer jedes Feindes Gut ertheilt.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬPraise verily at present, son of Vya┼Ыva, praise (Indra), who is the tenth of the pervading (vitalprinciples), the adorable, the all-wise to be honoured repeatedly (by sacred rites).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Vital principles: da┼Ыaman =the tenth; there are nine vital airs in the human body, Indra is the tenth; nava vai puruс╣гe pr─Бс╣З─Б manuс╣гyeс╣гuvartam─Бn─Б indras teс╣г─Бm da┼Ыadha; cf. Taittir─лya Br─Бhmaс╣Зa 1.3.7.4; Taittir─лya Saс╣Гhit─Б 1.7.9

Jamison Brereton

In just this way now, o Vaiya┼Ыva, praise him anew [/to the nines, and then] a tenth timeтАФ
the one who knows well, worthy to be celebrated by those who roam.

Jamison Brereton Notes

A very cute pun, with n├бvam meaning, as often in a hymnal context, тАШanewтАЩ, but in conjunction with da┼Ыam├бm тАШtenthтАЩ evoking n├бva тАШnineтАЩ.

car├бс╣Зi- is a hapax, but most likely derived from the root тИЪcar тАШwanderтАЩ (see EWA s.v. CARI , though AiG II.2.207 considers it of unclear meaning). It must have been created to contrast semantically with the very frequent near-rhyme form carс╣гaс╣З├н- тАШsettled/boundaried peoplesтАЩ, whose gen. pl. carс╣гaс╣З─лn─Б╠Бm occurs 35x in the RV, always at the end of the p─Бda as here (including VIII.23.7 h├│t─Бram carс╣гaс╣З─лn─Б╠Бm, the adjacent hymn by the same poet). That the short initial syllable of car├бс╣З─лn─Бm produces a bad cadence surely draws more attention to the word it was created in opposition to.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬIndra, of goodly aspect, bring to the offerer (of the oblation) that (protection) wherewith to defend himyou have twice slain (the goe) for Kutsa; show the same (care of us).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Bring to us that protection wherewith (youprotect your) offerer; send to us (that protection wherewith) you have twice slain (the foe) for Kutsa

Jamison Brereton

Bring that help here, Indra, with which, o most wondrous one, (you are there) for the (ritually) active man.
Once again pierce (┼Ъuс╣гс╣Зa?) for Kutsa and force (him) down.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Elliptical and with some syntactic puzzles. See Oldenberg on the verse in general and the multiple solutions proposed in earlier lit.

In b I supply тАЬbe thereтАЭ as the verb; Geldner, to more or less the same effect, тАЬbeistandest.тАЭ In c I supply ┼Ъuс╣гс╣Зa as the object of both verbs, since he is the demon Indra ordinarily slays for Kutsa. The problem here is that the verbs are not parallel: injunctive ┼Ыi┼Ыnathaс╕е followed by imperative n├н codaya. Somewhat reluctantly I ascribe imperatival value to ┼Ыi┼Ыnathaс╕е (so also Geldner without comment), possible because of the functional shape-shifting ability of injunctives. (See the same form in VIII.70.10.) However, I am not certain how often regular injunctives can show imperatival value, as opposed to lexicalized forms like d─Б╠Бс╕е and dh─Б╠Бс╕е. The root тИЪcud does not otherwise appear with n├н, a fact that makes its value here even less clear. Geldner supplies тАЬhorsesтАЭ as object, while Oldenberg suggests importing ├бvaс╕е тАШhelpтАЩ from a.

Griffith

O Indra, bring that aid wherewith of old, Most Wondrous! thou didst slay
His foes for active Kutsa: send it down to us.

Geldner

Dieselbe Hilfe bring, Indra, mit, der du gr├╢├Яter Meister dem Unternehmenden beistandest. Sto├Я nochmals f├╝r Kutsu zu, treib die Rosse an!

Grassmann

Die H├╝lfen bring, o Indra, her, durch die dem th├дt’gen Kutsa du Die Feinde schlugst, o herrlicher, die f├╝hr uns zu.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬ(Indra) of goodly aspect, we implore you who are entitled to praise, for (our) preservation; for you arethe overcomer of all our adversaries.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

We beg you now for a new (life?) for an older (man), o most wondrous one.
You are victorious over all our antagonistsтАФ

Jamison Brereton Notes

Again elliptical. In ab the semantic opposition between new and old is obviously the point, but what new thing are we begging Indra for? Geldner supplies тАЬdeedтАЭ (тАЬтАж eine (Tat), die auch dem ├Дlteste neu istтАЭ). In III.31.19 the same expression n├бvyam тАж s├бnyase refers to the making of a new hymn, but it makes no sense to beg Indra for a new hymn. I tentatively supply ─Б╠Бyuс╕е тАШlifeтАЩ, which occurs several times with n├бvyam (I.10.11, III.53.16, VII.80.2). The other occurrence of n├бvyaс╣Г sanyas├й (VIII.67.18) is found immediately after a periphrastic causative тАЬyou make liveтАЭ (VIII.67.17c d├йv─Бс╕е kс╣Ыс╣Зuth├б j─лv├бse), and a тАЬnew lifeтАЭ works reasonably well in that passage. But this is all circumstantial, and I do not know why such a wish would be expressed here, beyond the usual Vedic desire to live a full and vigorous lifetime.

The s├б tv├бm in c does not conform to the rules for 2nd ps. s├б reference developed in Jamison 1992. I would therefore prefer to supply an imperative тАЬ(be) victorious тАж,тАЭ which would, I think, also fit the context better. However, the offending s├б might be explained by the 3rd ps. verb (muc├бt) in the following verse (27ab), whose relative clauses hang off 26c, in my view. In other words, the construction of the whole sentence fluctuates between 2nd and 3rd ps. subject.

Griffith

So now we seek thee fresh in might, Most Wonderful in act! for gain:
For thou art he who conquers all our foes for us.

Geldner

Dich nur bitten wir jetzt um eine Tat, die auch dem ├Дltesten neu ist, du gr├╢├Яter Meister. Du bew├дltigst alle unsere Nachsteller;

Grassmann

Darum begehren wir von dir zum alten neues, herrlicher, Sei du Vertilger aller Widersacher uns.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬ(He it is) who rescues men from the wickedness of evil beings, who enriches (the dwellers) on theseven rivers; now hurl, you who abound in wealth, your weapon at the D─Бsa.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Dwelleres on the seven rivers:sapta sindhuс╣гu, i.e. the dwellers on the banks of the seven rivers; or, on the shores of the seven seas

Jamison Brereton

(You, the one) who releases (us) from the bear and from constraint or who (releases constraint) from the ─Аrya amid the seven rivers.
You have made the D─БsaтАЩs weapon bow, o you of powerful manliness.

Jamison Brereton Notes

As noted just above, I take the relative clauses in ab as hanging off 26c.

Both Geldner and Oldenberg make 27bc into a single clause, but the verb in c (n─лnamaс╕е) is unaccented although b begins with a relative pronoun y├бс╕е. I therefore take ab as being two parallel relative clauses sharing a single verb muc├бt; cleverly the poet has exploited the fact that тИЪmuc participates in two different syntactic constructions with accusative and ablative: тАЬrelease ROPE vel sim. [acc.] from VICTIM [abl.]тАЭ and тАЬrelease VICTIM [acc.] from ROPE [abl.].тАЭ (Perhaps not surprisingly, English has the same two constructions.) In 27a we find the first, though without overt expression of the VICTIM (=us or perhaps the ─Аrya); cf., e.g., X.97.15 t─Б╠Бno mu├▒cantu ├бс╣Гhasaс╕е. In b we find the second, though without overt expression of the ROPE. Here I supply ├бс╣Гhaс╕е adapted from abl. ├бс╣Гhasaс╕е in p─Бda a. Cf. IV.12.6=X.126.8 ev├│ с╣гv ├аsm├бn [i.e., asm├бt] mu├▒cata vy ├бс╣Гhaс╕е.

English translation:

тАЬAs you, Varu, have distributed vast wealth to those who have solicited (riches) on behalf of Sus─Бman,(so do you now distribute) to the descendants of Vya┼Ыva; (and so too you), auspicious food-bestowing (Uс╣гas).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

On behalf of Suс╣г─Бman: Varu is said to have distributed these alms that his father, Suс╣г─Бman, might go toheaven;

Uс╣гas: subhage v─Бjin─лvati: Uс╣гas is added, on the authority of ┼Ъaunaka; or, Varu himself addressedthe stanza to Uс╣гas and asks her to give him wealth for the sons of Vya┼Ыva, as she had given to his father for hissuppliants

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMay the gifts of a humane (price), when offering the Soma libation, extend to the Vya┼Ыvas, yes, andsubstantial wealthy by hundreds and thousands.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

N─Бrya = narahitasy─Бpatyam

Jamison Brereton

(Even so) let the priestly gift of N─Бrya come to the Vya┼Ыvas, who provide soma,
as well as substantial generosity in hundreds and thousands.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The adj. som├нnaс╕е can of course be either abl.-gen. sg. or nom.-acc. pl. It shares a p─Бda with acc. vy├а┼Ыv─Бn, so proximity favors taking it with that noun - as in the published translation (also Geldner). However, S─Бyaс╣Зa. takes it with gen. n─Бry├бsya in the previous p─Бda, and he may be correct. N─Бrya appears to be the (or one) name of the patron of the sacrifice, the dispenser of the dakс╣гiс╣З─Б to the poets, and it would make sense to refer to him as possessing or providing soma. I would therefore entertain the alternative tr.

тАЬ let the priestly gift of N─Бrya, provider of soma, come to the Vya┼Ыvas.тАЭ

Griffith

Let Narya’s sacrificial meed reach Vyasva’s Soma-bearing sons:
In hundreds and in thousands be the great reward.

Geldner

Die Schenkung des Narya soll zu den somafeiernden Vyasva┬┤s kommen und zwar eine stattliche Ehrengabe, eine hundertf├дltige, tausendf├дltige.

Grassmann

Des N─Бria Opferlohn komme zu den mit Soma versehenen Via├зva’s, und sein wuchtiges, hundertfaches, tausendfaches Geschenk.

Elizarenkova

рдЗрджрд╛рдиреАрдореБрд╖рд╕рдВ рд╕рдВрдмреЛрдзреНрдпрд╛рднрд┐рдзреАрдпрддреЗ ред рд╣реЗ рдХреБрд╣рдпрд╛рдХреГрддреЗ рд╕ рд╡рд░реБрдГ рдХреБрд╣ рдХреБрддреНрд░ рддрд┐рд╖реНрдарддреАрддреНрдпреЗрддрджрд┐рдЪреНрдЫрдпрд╛ рдЕрднрд┐рд▓рдХреНрд╖рдгрдкреНрд░рд╡реГрддреНрддреИрд░реНрдЬрд┐рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рд╕реБрднрд┐рдГ рдкреБрд░рд╕реНрдХреГрддреЗ ред рдХреБрд╣рд╢рдмреНрджрд╛рддреН рдХреНрдпрдЪреН ред рдПрддрд╛рджреГрд╢реЗ рд╣реЗ рдЙрд╖рдГ рддреНрд╡рд╛ рддреНрд╡рд╛рдВ рдпрддреН рдпрджрд╛ рдХрд╢реНрдЪрд┐рддреН рдкреГрдЪреНрдЫрд╛рддреН рдкреГрдЪреНрдЫрддрд┐ рдИрдЬрд╛рдирдГ рдЗрд╖реНрдЯрд╡рд╛рдиреН рд╡рд░реБрдГ рдХреБрд╣рдпрд╛ рдХреНрд╡ рддрд┐рд╖реНрдарддреАрддрд┐ рдпрджрд╛ рдкреГрдЪреНрдЫрддрд┐ рддрджрд╛рдиреАрдореН рдЕрдкрд╢реНрд░рд┐рддрдГ рд╕рд░реНрд╡реИрд░рд╛рд╢реНрд░рд┐рддрдГ ред рдпрджреНрд╡рд╛ ред рд╡рд┐рд╡реГрддрджреНрд╡рд╛рд░рдГ ред рдпрджрд╛ рдпрд╛рдЪрдорд╛рдирд╛ рдЖрдЧрдЪреНрдЫрдиреНрддрд┐ рддрджрд╛ рджреМрд╡рд╛рд░рд┐рдХрд╛ рдиреЗ рдкреНрд░рддрд┐рдмрдзреНрдирдиреНрддреАрддреНрдпрд░реНрдердГ ред рддрд╛рджреГрд╢рдГ рд╡рд▓рдГ рд╡рд░рдГ рд╕реНрд╡рдмрд▓реЗрдирд╛рд╡рд╛рд░рдХрдГ рд╢рддреНрд░реВрдгрд╛рдореН ред рдпрджреНрд╡рд╛ ред рднрд┐рдХреНрд╖реВрдгрд╛рдВ рдзрдирд╛рджрд┐рдкреНрд░рджрд╛рдиреЗрдирд╛рд╡рд░рд┐рддрд╛ ред рдПрд╖реЛ рдПрд╖ рд╡рд░реБрдГ рдЧреЛрдорддреАрдореН рдПрддрдиреНрдирд╛рдорд┐рдХрд╛рдВ рдирджреАрдореН ред ‘рдХрд╛рд▓рд╛рдзреНрд╡рдиреЛ: ’ рдЗрддрд┐ рджреНрд╡рд┐рддреАрдпрд╛ ред рддрд╕реНрдпрд╛рд╕реНрддреАрд░реЗ рдЕрд╡ рддрд┐рд╖реНрдарддрд┐ рдЗрддрд┐ рддрджрд╛рдиреАрдВ рддреНрд╡рдВ рдХрдердпрд╕рд┐ рее рее реиреж рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬIf any ask of you, (Uс╣гas), when anywhere present, where the sacrificer (Varu dwells), (reply) thepowerful (prince), the refuge of all, abides on (the banks of) the Gomat─л river.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Ask of you: kuhay─Бkс╣Ыte = oс╕е,you who are honoured by those who ask where Varu wells, sa varuс╕е kutra tiс╣гс╣нhattyetad icchay─Бbhilakс╣гaс╣Зapravс╣Ыttair jij├▒─Бsubhiс╕е puraskс╣Ыte (uс╣гas);

Valaс╕е = varaс╕е, svabalena av─Бrakaс╕е ┼Ыatr┼лс╣З─Бm, overwhelmer ofenemies

Jamison Brereton

When the sacrificer will ask you: тАЬWhere (is he), you where-actor?тАЭ (you will answer:) тАЬThis тАШValaтАЩ [=the patron Varo Suс╣г─Бman], who is set apart, is descending toward the Gomat─л (River) [/pen full of cows].тАЭ

Jamison Brereton Notes

In contrast to the first two fairly straightforward verses of the d─Бnastuti (28-29), this one bristles with slangy jokes and their attendant puzzles. It is also the only verse in the hymn not in Uс╣гс╣Зih meter. The verse opens with the sacrificer (─лj─Бn├бс╕е, lit. the pf. mid. participle to тИЪyaj) asking тАЬyouтАЭ an abrupt question kuhay─Б╠Б kuhay─Бkс╣Ыte, consisting of an extended form of k├║ha тАШwhereтАЩ (the extended form found only here) and an oddly formed, nonce vocative made up of the same adverbial interrogative plus (probably) -kс╣Ыti- (though -kс╣Ыt─Б- would also be possible). Judging from vs. 28, the beginning of the d─Бnastuti, which contains a vocative addressed to Dawn, she is also the addressee here, though a reversion to the default Indra is certainly not excluded. So, literally, тАЬwhere? you where-actor.тАЭ Geldner takes ─лj─Бn├бс╕е as the subject of the question (тАЬwhere is the sacrificer?тАЭ), rather than the questioner. I follow Oldenberg: тАЬDie Opferer fragt die Morgenr├╢te тАж,тАЭ although GeldnerтАЩs interpretation is by no means excluded. The question is whether Varosuс╣г─Бman is the sacrificer himself or his patron, and without a better knowledge of the distribution of roles in RVic sacrifice, we cannot know for sure.

It is generally assumed (I think correctly) that the second hemistich is the response of the addressee to the question in ab, and it is an extended pun. He calls the subject, about whose whereabouts the question was just asked, тАЬVala,тАЭ that is, the name of IndraтАЩs opponent and the cave that contained the stolen cows. But Vala is also a phonological variant of Vara, the first part of the name of the patron Varosuс╣г─Бman. He is said to be тАЬset apartтАЭ (├бpa┼Ыritaс╕е) along the Gomat─л (River), but g├│mant- literally means тАШpossessing cattleтАЩ and can also qualify the Vala cave itself (see I.11.5 val├бsya g├│mataс╕е). Thus this line appears to be a subtle reminder to Varosuс╣г─Бman not to withhold his cattle within himself, like his phonological multiform, but to be generous to his clients. The whole line reminds us of the d─Бnastuti in V.61.19: eс╣г├б kс╣гeti r├бthav─лtir magh├бv─Б g├│mat─лr ├бnu, p├бrveteс╣гv ├бpa┼Ыritaс╕е “This Rathav─лti dwells in peace, a bounteous patron throughout the cow-rich (clans) [/along the Gomat─л river], set back among the mountains,” containing one of the only two other occurrences of ├бpa┼Ыrita. I do not know the significance of this.

Griffith

If one should ask thee, Where is he who sacrificed? Whither lookest thou?
Like Vala he hath passed away and dwelleth now on Gomati.

Geldner

Wenn man dich fragen sollte: Wo ist der Opferherr, o du ├╝berall Wirkende, so sollst du sagen: Dieser Vala hat sich zur├╝ckgezogen und steigt zur Gomati hinab.

Grassmann

Wenn dich ein Opfernder fragen sollte: Wo bist du, wo wirkest du, [so sprich:] Dieser Vala, der sich versteckt hat, geht herab zum Gomati-Strome.

Elizarenkova
